There are\\n69:     no implicit dependencies between numbered migrations - the numbering is\\n70:     merely a convention to aid file listing. Every new numbered migration\\n71:     has a declared dependency to the previous number, meaning that VCS\\n72:     branch merges can be detected and resolved.\\n73: \\n74:     Migrations files can be marked as replacing another set of migrations -\\n75:     this is to support the \\\"squash\\\" feature. The graph handler isn't\\n76:     responsible for these; instead, the code to load them in here should\\n77:     examine the migration files and if the replaced migrations are all either\\n78:     unapplied or not present, it should ignore the replaced ones, load in just\\n79:     the replacing migration, and repoint any dependencies that pointed to the\\n80:     replaced migrations to point to the replacing one.\\n81: \\n82:     A node should be a tuple: (app_path, migration_name). The tree\\n83:     special-cases things within an app - namely, root nodes and leaf nodes\\n84:     ignore dependencies to other apps.\\n85:     \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n86: \\n87:     def __init__(self):\\n88:         self.node_map = {}\\n89:         self.nodes = {}\\n90: \\n91:     def add_node(self, key, migration):\\n92:         assert key not in self.node_map\\n93:         node = Node(key)\\n94:         self.node_map[key] = node\\n95:         self.nodes[key] = migration\\n96: \\n97:     def add_dummy_node(self, key, origin, error_message):\\n98:         node = DummyNode(key, origin, error_message)\\n99:         self.node_map[key] = node\\n100:         self.nodes[key] = None\\n101: \\n102:     def add_dependency(self, migration, child, parent, skip_validation=False):\\n103:         \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n104:         This may create dummy nodes if they don't yet exist. Any\\n128:         dependencies that were referencing them are changed to reference the\\n129:         `replacement` node instead.\\n130:         \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n131:         # Cast list of replaced keys to set to speed up lookup later.\\n132:         replaced = set(replaced)\\n133:         try:\\n134:             replacement_node = self.node_map[replacement]\\n135:         except KeyError as err:\\n136:             raise NodeNotFoundError(\\n137:                 \\\"Unable to find replacement node %r. It was either never added\\\"\\n138:                 \\\" to the migration graph, or has been removed.\\\" % (replacement,),\\n139:                 replacement,\\n140:             ) from err\\n141:         for replaced_key in replaced:\\n142:             self.nodes.pop(replaced_key, None)\\n143:             replaced_node = self.node_map.pop(replaced_key, None)\\n144:             if replaced_node:\\n145:                 for child in replaced_node.children:\\n146:                     child.parents.remove(replaced_node)\\n147:                     # We don't want to create dependencies between the replaced\\n148:                     # node and the replacement node as this would lead to\\n149:                     # self-referencing on the replacement node at a later\\n150:                     # iteration.\\n151:                     if child.key not in replaced:\\n152:                         replacement_node.add_child(child)\\n153:                         child.add_parent(replacement_node)\\n154:                 for parent in replaced_node.parents:\\n155:                     parent.children.remove(replaced_node)\\n156:                     # Again, to avoid self-referencing.\\n157:                     if parent.key not in replaced:\\n158:                         replacement_node.add_parent(parent)\\n159:                         parent.add_child(replacement_node)\\n160: \\n161:     def remove_replacement_node(self, replacement, replaced):\\n162:         \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n163:         The inverse operation to `remove_replaced_nodes`. Almost. Remove the\\n164:         replacement node `replacement` and remap its child nodes to `replaced`\\n165:         - the list of nodes it would have replaced.
